### 5. Demonstrate Vector DBs and Use Cases

#### Vector DB1: E-commerce RecSys
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=0)** In the last chapter, we spoke about the scalability of a vector database and assessing its performance.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=5)** In this chapter, we'll introduce three different and common uses of vector databases in industry, starting off with building a recommender system.
>
> **[0:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=15)** So, let's think about what a recommender system is.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=18)** So, if you look at my screen, you can think of this as an e-commerce platform where if a user comes in, and they're interested in buying a particular product, let's say we're here and we're interested in buying this shirt, for example.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=30)** What you'd like to do is if a user shows interest in this by clicking it, or by putting this particular item in their cart, you want to reorganize all of the products that you have on your storefront so that similar items are shown further up, because now the user has shown you their intention of what they're interested in, and you can then recommend similar items to them.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=54)** And so, in order to do this, you can use a vector database to build the underlying infrastructure for that. Let's have a look at how we can do that.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=62)** The idea here is if we want to recommend an item, we need to know who's asking.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=69)** So, if I am asking you to recommend to me, a blue shirt versus somebody else asking for a blue shirt, depending on my likes and my dislikes, the blue shirt that I'm interested in might be different.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=79)** So, you have to establish who's asking to build a good recommender system.
>
> **[1:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=83)** So, the way we do that is by encoding multiple classes.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=86)** You need a user class, you need products and you need brands.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=91)** And so, once you've got those three isolated classes, then what you can do is establish vectorized representations of each one of those.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=100)** So, for example, for the product class, we can establish the vectorized representation for the product by encoding its image and creating a vector for the image so we can display similar products.
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=111)** Then, we can use this property of Weaviate, known as cross-references, which are shown here in the diagram as arrows.
>
> **[1:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=118)** And so, if you create a user, that user can like a particular product, and that can be encoded in the database schema as a cross-reference from the user class to the product class.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=128)** Similarly, the product can also have a brand so that exists as a cross-reference between the product class and the brand class.
>
> **[2:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=136)** And the reason why we need these cross-references is because establishing the vectors for the individual classes will then be easy to do.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=144)** So, using these cross-references or graph-references, we can actually capture user interest.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=149)** So, let's say I'm a user here, and I have interacted with two items on your e-commerce storefront.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=155)** I've bought a shirt, and I've bought a pair of boots.
>
> **[2:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=158)** What we're going to do is represent a user's interest by drawing a graph-reference, or a cross-reference from the user class to the products that that user has interacted with.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=170)** And so, the user and the product classes' interaction can be used to establish recommendations personalized to that user.
>
> **[2:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=178)** These cross-references can be established as a result of a user liking an item, putting that item into their online cart, or even buying that item.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=187)** And so, the way we use these cross-references is using a module called Ref2Vec, which allows us to turn a reference into a vector.
>
> **[3:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=196)** So, for example, let's say you have a user over here and they like this shirt and this pair of boots.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=203)** You can use these references, these arrows to establish a vector for that user, which is a function of the products that they like.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=212)** And so, this user likes the shirt and the pair of boots, we can take the product and their vector representations, and then we can create an up to date vector representation of the user as an average of the shirt vector and an average of the boot vector.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=228)** And so, effectively, what we're doing here is, in real-time, accounting for the fact that a user's preferences can change, and we're updating their vector by averaging all of the products that they like in real-time.
>
> **[4:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=241)** And you can scale this up to millions of items, and you can do real-time recommendations as a result of this.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=247)** So, the minute somebody logs into your e-commerce platform, they click a couple of items, you can take the average of the vector of those items and rerank everything on your storefront to be similar to the items that the user likes.
>
> **[4:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=260)** Effectively, the products that the user chooses to interact with on your platform, then define the identity or define the vector of that user and that is used to perform recommendations to that user.
>
> **[4:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=271)** And this is unique to every user that logs on to your platform.
>
> **[4:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=274)** So, it's personalization at the user level.
>
> **[4:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=277)** So, for this, what we're going to be using is the Ref2Vec e-commerce demo that's built on top of Weaviate and by Weaviate.
>
> **[4:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=283)** So, we've created this, and effectively, what we have to do here is two things.
>
> **[4:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=289)** We need to establish the references within our schema, which I'll show first of all over here.
>
> **[4:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=295)** So, if we look at one of the code files where locally deploying Weaviate as we've done before, but now we're creating two classes.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=302)** The first class we're going to create is the product class.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=305)** And the product class uses a multi2Vec-clip module.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=309)** And here, it only has an image field.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=311)** So, effectively, you can tell from this that the vector for the product is going to be generated by looking at the image of that product.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=319)** If we go down and if we look at the properties that the product has, it has the image that's going to be used to vectorize the product.
>
> **[5:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=325)** It has a description, the text, the name of the product, it has where that product's images are stored.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=332)** It has a location of the SKU number.
>
> **[5:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=335)** We've got category for that product.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=337)** We've got multiple pieces of information.
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=340)** But the main piece here is that a product's vector is established as a result of its image.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=346)** The next thing if we scroll down in the schema definition is the definition of a user class.
>
> **[5:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=351)** So, anytime somebody logs on to your platform, you create a new user for that person.
>
> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=357)** And interestingly, how we establish the cross-reference here is notice how one of the properties for the user class is a liked item, and the type of this is a product.
>
> **[6:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=368)** So, the type here is not a blob or a text string or anything like that.
>
> **[6:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=372)** In fact, it is a instance of another class of type product over here.
>
> **[6:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=378)** And so, here, effectively, when you do this, what you're telling Weaviate, the vector database is every time a user interacts with a product that is going to point to another class, and that's going to link it to that user's class, and this is how we generate those arrows that we just spoke about.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=397)** The next thing that we're going to do is take this and tell the Weaviate module how to determine a vector for the user, which is through the ref2vec-centroid module. And the ref2vec-centroid module takes the references for that user, in this case, all of the products that that user likes, and it uses those to generate a vector for that user.
>
> **[6:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=416)** And this is how we know what individual users like.
>
> **[7:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=420)** The next thing we're going to do is go ahead and upload all of this data to Weaviate.
>
> **[7:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=424)** So, we're going to upload the image of the product, we're going to upload the label name, the category, the description, all of that, including the image being encoded.
>
> **[7:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=433)** And then, once that's all ready to go, we're going to go ahead and show you what that e-commerce platform looks like with this recommender system enabled now.
>
> **[7:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=445)** So, here in my platform, I've organized all of my products and I can see that blue shirt that I'm interested in.
>
> **[7:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=452)** There's two functionalities that I want to demonstrate here.
>
> **[7:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=454)** First of all, I can search over products.
>
> **[7:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=457)** So, this is the first feature that a vector database enables.
>
> **[7:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=460)** So, I can, for example, say that I'm only interested in half-sleeve shirts.
>
> **[7:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=465)** So, I can enable that, and I can perform that search.
>
> **[7:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=468)** So, now I get these half-sleeved shirts that are organized to be at the top.
>
> **[7:52](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=472)** Let's say I pick a product that I'm interested in, this blue shirt that I initially showed you on the storefront.
>
> **[7:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=477)** I click that. As soon as I click that, it's now re-ranked all of the product offerings so that it shows me what's more similar to this shirt.
>
> **[8:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=486)** So, if I'm interested in this blue shirt, potentially, I could be interested in this other blue shirt.
>
> **[8:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=490)** And now, if you imagine if we had thousands of product offerings, as soon as a user shows you their intent of what product they're interested in, you can use a vector database to establish what type of shirt they're interested in by taking the vector of that shirt, and then reorganizing all of the other products to establish what other products have vectors close to that, and then reordering what they're seeing in real-time.
>
> **[8:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=514)** And that increases the chances that they're going to find what they're interested in.
>
> **[8:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=518)** That increases the conversion rate to buying that product.
>
> **[8:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=521)** And this scales from just a few images in this toy example, all the way up to hundreds of thousands of unique product offerings.
>
> **[8:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=529)** And that's the power of a vector database being used to power your recommender system on your e-commerce platform.
>
> **[8:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=535)** And this is one of the main critical applications of vector databases that are used in industry currently.
>
> **[9:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=542)** Here, we saw how you can make real time recommendations as customers are navigating an e-commerce platform.
>
> **[9:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db1-e-commerce-recsys?u=76281980&t=548)** In the next video, we'll see a different flavor of search that vector databases enable called hybrid search.

> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=284)** And this is telling you a story.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=286)** What this is saying is that you've asked directly for a keyword match for the word animal, and it couldn't find more than one.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=293)** And the one that it found here, if we read the question weighing around a ton, this eland is the largest species of this animal in Africa.
>
> **[5:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=301)** So, here, the word animal matches with our query and therefore this question gets returned.
>
> **[5:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=307)** Notice how for the other three here, elephant, this is conceptually related to our query, and so is this.
>
> **[5:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=314)** But these are not returned because the keywords do not line up.
>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=317)** And we can't find the keyword animal in these two queries.
>
> **[5:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=321)** So, that's the main idea behind keyword search.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=323)** It only returns objects if the words exactly match.
>
> **[5:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=327)** In practice, what we'd ideally like is to merge these two types of searches.
>
> **[5:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=332)** We want to be able to perform keyword search and semantic search and then say, I want some hybrid or some fusion of these two results.
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=340)** And that's known as hybrid search.
>
> **[5:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=342)** So, how can we perform hybrid search or get the best of both worlds.
>
> **[5:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=346)** So, to do that with Weaviate, we have to slightly change the query again.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=350)** So, what I'm going to do is rather than rewrite the query again, I'm going to take this query and I'm going to show you how to modify it to turn it into a hybrid search query.
>
> **[5:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=358)** So, we're going to paste that in here.
>
> **[6:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=360)** And then now we're not doing a keyword search here.
>
> **[6:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=363)** So, I'm going to delete that portion of the query, and I'm going to go ahead and show you what the hybrid search query looks like.
>
> **[6:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=369)** So, here, I'm going to do with hybrid, and now we can pass in the query again.
>
> **[6:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=376)** So, the query here is going to stay the same animal.
>
> **[6:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=379)** And we can also specify this alpha parameter here.
>
> **[6:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=382)** And we'll talk about what that is in a second.
>
> **[6:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=384)** Let's just run this, and we'll look at the results.
>
> **[6:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=388)** So, now, we asked for three results.
>
> **[6:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=391)** We're getting three results.
>
> **[6:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=393)** Notice how the three results are exactly the same as vector search.
>
> **[6:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=397)** But what's a little different now is the ordering of the three results.
>
> **[6:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=401)** So, what I'm going to do is go back up to the vector search results.
>
> **[6:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=405)** In this, we had elephant, and we have the crocodile result, and then, we had the antelope result.
>
> **[6:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=410)** The ordering now is slightly different.
>
> **[6:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=413)** The antelope is at the highest ranking, then we have elephant, then we have the concept of this crocodile question.
>
> **[7:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=420)** This reordering is significant here.
>
> **[7:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=422)** It might seem small, but it's significant.
>
> **[7:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=424)** The reason why it got reordered was because if you look at how highly antelope was rated by vector search, if we scroll up here, it was last.
>
> **[7:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=434)** But when we're doing hybrid search, we're doing both keyword search and vector search.
>
> **[7:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=439)** So, vector search doesn't give antelope a lot of significance.
>
> **[7:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=443)** But let's have a look at keyword search.
>
> **[7:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=444)** So, keyword search returned only antelope.
>
> **[7:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=447)** So, according to keyword search this is the most important concept.
>
> **[7:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=451)** So, when we do hybrid search, we take both of them and we say which of these results is the most important based on both types of searches, which is why antelope, this question gets re-ranked and gets put in at the highest priority here, and the other two results get pushed down to the second and third place.
>
> **[7:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=470)** And this is the idea behind fusing or taking a hybrid between keyword search and vector search.
>
> **[7:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=476)** The last thing that I want to talk about here is what happens when I modify this alpha parameter.
>
> **[8:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=481)** The way to understand the alpha parameter is by understanding it as the strength of vector search.
>
> **[8:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=487)** So, if I set this to completely zero.
>
> **[8:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=490)** So, if alpha is equal to zero, this will purely be keyword search.
>
> **[8:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=494)** So, I have vector search strength of zero.
>
> **[8:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=496)** So, if I run this, I get pure keyword search.
>
> **[8:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=500)** This is the exact same result as when I run bm25.
>
> **[8:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=503)** And when I go to the other end, when I say I want pure vector search alpha of one, all of the weighting is given to vector search.
>
> **[8:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=511)** If I rerun that now, I get pure vector search.
>
> **[8:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=516)** So, you can balance between keyword search and vector search by modifying alpha to control which works best in practice.
>
> **[8:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=526)** Here we introduced hybrid search, which allows you to tune how much you want to match exact words versus concepts in the return results.
>
> **[8:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db2-hybrid-search?u=76281980&t=535)** In the next video, we'll talk about another wildly popular application of vector databases, using them to improve large language models like ChatGPT.

#### Vector DB3: Retrieval augmented generation
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=0)** Now, let's talk about how you can use a vector database to improve a large language model-based chatbot like chat GPT.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=7)** The problem with large language models like ChatGPT is that they don't know anything they haven't been trained on. Using the information stored in a vector database, we can solve this problem.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=18)** Retrieval-Augmented Generation, RAG, is a technique that allows you to tell your large language model about relevant concepts prior to getting it to answer a question.
>
> **[0:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=28)** This is how RAG works.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=30)** First, we query the vector database with a concept.
>
> **[0:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=33)** Second, we obtain retrieved results from semantic search, then, we build a prompt that uses these retrieve results, and we feed that prompt and results into the large language model to generate from.
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=46)** This allows a large language model to read retrieved relevant facts before having to generate an answer to a question, very much in the same manner as you would go to research a topic prior to writing an essay, or providing a well-thought out answer.

> **[4:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=285)** We're going to limit it so that this only happens with two objects, and we're going to allow it to perform this.
>
> **[4:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=294)** And this is the whole retrieval augmented generation workflow.
>
> **[4:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=299)** You retrieve the objects and then you generate.
>
> **[5:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=302)** So, that's the whole concept of retrieval augmented generation.
>
> **[5:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=305)** So, let's run this query, and we'll have a look at what happens.
>
> **[5:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=309)** And as this query is being run, it's running the vector search that extracts our two concepts, these two concepts.
>
> **[5:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=316)** And then it's calling an endpoint that is, sending those and our prompt to a large language model to then generate an answer.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=323)** That's why this particular one takes longer than all of the other previous ones that we've seen so far.
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=329)** So, we've got the answerback.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=331)** And so, here, this is the story of an elephant flying, and this is written by a large language model.
>
> **[5:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=337)** You can read over this.
>
> **[5:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=338)** It's pretty interesting.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=339)** But this is the power of retrieval augmented generation, the ability to control the generation from a large language model using context provided by retrieved information from a vector database.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=350)** And so here the context is elephant.
>
> **[5:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=353)** And then again, you have a second story where here the context is the nose or snout.
>
> **[5:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=359)** So, in order to generate correct stories, you have to make sure that the retrieved concepts are correctly referenced in the prompt as well.
>
> **[6:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=366)** Where here, this seems to be a more correct prompting, then this second prompting.
>
> **[6:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=373)** So, the next thing that we're going to show you is how to perform prompt over large amounts of returned objects.
>
> **[6:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=381)** And the way we do this is by performing grouped tasks.
>
> **[6:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=385)** So, here, let's say we return all ten objects from our database.
>
> **[6:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=390)** We go in, we get all the different categories back, we get animals science.
>
> **[6:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=395)** There's only two different categories that we have amongst our ten questions.
>
> **[6:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=399)** So, we get all of them back, and we're only extracting category here.
>
> **[6:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=402)** So, we're not extracting the question or the answer.
>
> **[6:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=406)** And this is because the prompt that we're going to write only has to do with the category.
>
> **[6:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=409)** So, you can only extract what you need and then specify that in the prompt.
>
> **[6:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=413)** So, in this prompt, what we're going to do is go in here, and we're going to say the prompt now is which of these subjects and the subjects are specified by the category, so it will be science, science, science, animals ten different iterations does a zoologist specialize in?
>
> **[7:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=439)** And that's our question to the large language model.
>
> **[7:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=442)** So we can write that prompt.
>
> **[7:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=445)** And then now we're going to take the query that we had here.
>
> **[7:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=449)** We're going to take this query, and we're going to modify it slightly.
>
> **[7:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=455)** Can I go in here?
>
> **[7:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=456)** And now, instead of just returning these results, we're going to add in a component here where we say with generate.
>
> **[7:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=465)** And this is a group task now because we're grouping all of the returned categories science, science, and animals.
>
> **[7:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=473)** And we want it to answer one question over all of those returned results.
>
> **[7:58](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=478)** So, we pass it the prompt here now and we get it to generate.
>
> **[8:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=481)** So, now what's happening here is it's generating one answer, but taking in all of the relevant ten pieces of information.
>
> **[8:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=489)** And the answer that it comes up with here is a zoologist specializes in this subject category of animals.
>
> **[8:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=495)** And here, it was given ten options.
>
> **[8:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=498)** So, it was given animals, animals, science.
>
> **[8:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=500)** There's two unique options but ten options in total, and it picked the right option.
>
> **[8:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=505)** Even though there's a little bit of fuzziness around, science could have also been correct, but it picked the more correct one.
>
> **[8:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=510)** And using this type of workflow, you can take the power of a large language model and control its generation to be grounded in context extracted from your vector database.
>
> **[8:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=521)** And this is one of the reasons why retrieval augmented generation is so popular, and people are using it in production.
>
> **[8:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=527)** Here, we introduce the topic of RAG, which allows chatbots to search over, read and cite relevant source material before having to answer prompts.
>
> **[8:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=537)** It even allows chatbots to answer questions about information they haven't directly been trained on.
>
> **[9:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/vector-db3-retrieval-augmented-generation?u=76281980&t=542)** We'll code up our RAG workflow in the next challenge.

The first time with this question, the second time with this question, and the third time with this question.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=247)** And then, it's going to ask the large language model to answer that question.
>

>

>

>

>

>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=284)** So, we can verify if these are the right answers.
>
> **[4:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=286)** To do that, we're going to go ahead and extract them out.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=290)** So, we're going to take our original query that we use to extract these questions out, and we're going to modify it slightly.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=296)** So, now, instead of just asking for the question, we're also going to ask for the answer.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=300)** So, we're just going to go ahead and modify this to ask for question and answer, like so.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=308)** Go ahead and run that.
>
> **[5:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=311)** So, now, we get the question and the corresponding answer.
>
> **[5:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=315)** Elephant, the nose or snout, and antelope.
>
> **[5:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=317)** And we can go ahead and verify.
>
> **[5:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=319)** So, the first answer was elephant and the large language model got it.
>
> **[5:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=323)** So, it says what is elephant?
>
> **[5:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=324)** So, that's one check.
>
> **[5:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=326)** The second answer was, what is its long, narrow snout?
>
> **[5:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=329)** And the correct answer is the nose or snout.
>
> **[5:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=331)** So, that's correct as well.
>
> **[5:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=333)** And the last answer, the correct answer was antelope.
>
> **[5:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=336)** And the large language model got it as well.
>
> **[5:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=339)** What is antelope?
>
> **[5:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=340)** So, this is pretty accurate.
>
> **[5:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=341)** Another thing that I would recommend you can do is give it all ten questions and see how many of those it can get right if you're interested in that.
>
> **[5:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=350)** In this final chapter, we introduced how vector databases can be used to build recommender systems in e-commerce and beyond.

> **[5:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/introduction-to-ai-native-vector-databases/solution-vector-dbs?u=76281980&t=357)** We also explored the concept of retrieval augmented generation, or RAG for short, that's being used along with large language models to power chatbots, agents, and search engines in production at multiple companies as we speak.
